*******************************************************************************
*
* Whilst this is essentially a TNP formatted file, it is designed as an input
* file for the ASSelect program.  To that end there are control lines in the
* data identified by '*FILTERTAG <label>'.  If you take the file 'as is' then
* the results are unpredictable.
*
* ASSelect decodes the Lat/Longs for OA translation and for geographical limits
* The parser is very simple so the formatting of the values must be exactly as
* shown (e.g. circle radius of 1/2 nm MUST BE represented as '00.50').
*
*******************************************************************************
*
* Sections are laid out in the sequence they occur within the UK AIP.
*
* Part 2 ENR section 2.1 - Air Traffic Services Airspace - TMAs etc
* Part 2 ENR section 2.2 - Other regulated Airspace - MATZs etc
* Part 2 ENR section 3.1 - Lower ATS routes - Airways
* Part 2 ENR section 3.2 - Upper ATS routes - Omitted (above FL195)
* Part 2 ENR section 3.6 - En-route holding - Empty at present
* Part 2 ENR section 5.1 - Danger Areas
* Part 2 ENR section 5.1 cont. - Prohibited Areas
* Part 2 ENR section 5.1 cont. - Restricted Areas
* Part 2 ENR section 5.2 - Military exercise and training areas - Wave boxes
* Part 2 ENR section 5.3 - Gas Venting Stations
* Part 2 ENR section 5.3 cont. - High Intensity Radio Transmission Areas
* Part 2 ENR section 5.3 cont. - Lasers
* Part 2 ENR section 5.4 - Air navigation obstacles - RTM and chimneys
* Part 2 ENR section 5.5 - Aerial Sporting and Recreational Activities
*       Hang Gliding omitted
*       Parachute Zones
*       Aerial Sporting (aka gliding clubs)
*       Ultra light flights
* Part 3 AD section 2.2 (elevation) + section 2.17 for airfields with ATZs
*
* There are lots of options on sectors which you can enable / disable - mainly
* with respect to Letters Of Agreement, but also with GVS, RTM, HIRTAs etc.
* You should check the file for what you want and not just take it "as is".
*
* Subsequent to the first issue of this file in early 2014, a program was written
* to perform the inc./exc. functions.  It uses a library of filtertags to analyse
* the file, present options to the user and configure an o/p file appropriately.
*
* Off-shore areas are omitted
* Non-mainland UK areas are omitted with a few exceptions (Isle of Wight)
* Areas above FL195 are incomplete
* Where an ATZ or other feature lies within a CTR it has been omitted
*
*******************************************************************************
*
* Letters of Agreement - these are problematical as firstly each one tends to
* be restricted to gliders flying from a particular club.  Secondly if a glider
* has access to one it doesn't necessarily get access to any others and thirdly
* flight navigation equipment doesn't have the ability to negate a section of
* airspace, this gives problems because the pilot won't get a warning when
* exiting an area permitted by a LoA into a wider 'not permitted' sector which
* they have already entered as part of the LoA.
*
* This file is therefore set-up as follows :
*
* For each LOA the user must elect to either include or exclude it.  Having
* made that decision, they must then switch various sectors ON or OFF by using
* the INCLUDE=YES or NO command.  These are grouped appropriately so the user
* only needs to search this file for their specific LOA(s).  If excluding the
* LOA, then the full sectors are enabled and the LOA sectors are disabled. If
* including the LOA, then the full sectors are disabled and the sectors are
* sub-divided into those sub-sectors which are inside or outside the LOA.  The
* sub-sectors are still listed with their appropriate CLASS and TYPE, but the
* TITLES of the sub-sectors within the agreed areas carry an LOA tag.  It
* would be nice if it could also list the name and the frequency but space is
* limited on moving map displays so only the name is included and pilots must
* find the frequency for themselves (which will encourage them to check the
* paperwork before they fly).  Also it requires more memory to implement most
* LOAs, so the default is usually to exclude them here unless it appears to be
* generally useful or if there is no memory penalty in including them (though
* most are implemented).
*
*                               Wave Boxes
*
* The LOA for TRA Areas 008, 007, 006, 005, and 004 hasn't been implemented.
*
* The LOA for TRA(G) with Annexes A through H has (excluding Northern Ireland)
*
* Wave boxes above FL195 are defined in two parts.  The box itself followed by
* slabs 1" wide around the sides and a slab 100' thick over the top. A box that
* starts above FL195 (e.g. FL240) is given a slab 100' thick under it. The slabs
* are there to ensure you get a warning if you wander to the edge of the box.
* Note that these slabs are OUTSIDE the boxes, they are not part of the boxes.
*
* Wave boxes are by default excluded - if you switch the leading INCLUDE to YES
* for a box (each box set needs to be enabled separately) you will also get the
* boundary slabs, unless you uncomment the embedded INCLUDE=NO.
*
*******************************************************************************
* Part 2 ENR section 2.1                                                      *
*  Air Traffic Services Airspace                                              *
*******************************************************************************

*
*
*
*
* MATZs The precise co-ordinates of these aren't laid down in the 
* AIPs, in general : circle 5nm radius unless otherwise stated, SFC to 3000AAL,
* stubs 5nm extra, from 1000AAL to 3000 AAL, 2nm either side of centre line.
* The stub length starts from the edge of the circle on the appropriate bearing
* from the ARP.
*
* The stubs have been derived by converting the airfield reference point to the
* UK National Grid, obtaining a local Grid North/True North difference at the
* ARP, performing the appropriate geometry to determine the corners of the
* stubs, and then reconverting back to WGS84. Where the stub of one MATZ
* intersected the circle of another MATZ, LXAsbrowser was used to determine the
* lat/long of that intersection and then the file was updated accordingly.
* Where 2 circles intersected and the ARPs of the original file matched the UK
* AIP, the intersecting points of the original file was kept (this was
* predominantly the case - so little time, so much to do).
*
* Barkston Heath
* notes: 3nm circle, stub SFC to 3000, 058T, length 2nm
* This defines 5nm circle on Cranwell, 3nm circle on Barkston and the
* stub on Barkston. The other stub on Cranwell is defined later.
* The high point is based on the higher of the two airfields.
AC G
AN BARKSTON CRANWELL:124.450
AL SFC
AH 3367ALT
DP 52:58:14 N 000:38:35 W
V D=+
V X=52:57:44 N 000:33:42 W
DB 52:58:14 N 000:38:35 W, 52:59:52 N 000:37:12 W
DP 52:59:52 N 000:37:12 W
V D=+
V X=53:01:48 N 000:29:34 W
DB 52:59:52 N 000:37:12 W, 52:56:49 N 000:28:58 W
DP 52:56:49 N 000:28:58 W
V D=+
V X=52:57:44 N 000:33:42 W
DB 52:56:49 N 000:28:58 W, 52:54:52 N 000:35:05 W
DP 52:53:23 N 000:38:57 W
DP 52:56:46 N 000:42:28 W
DP 52:58:14 N 000:38:35 W
*

* This section of the AIPs defines the airways.  They are defined as a centre
* line point, bearing, distance and width, with some coincident.  The AIPs also
* include a graphic display of the result.  This file has used earlier files
* checked against the AIP graphics, with spreadsheet generated data for those
* airways in the graphics but not in the earlier files.
*
* Note that they are not all Class A
* Airways extension above FL195 have been omitted
* Airways embedded in other Controlled Airspace have been omitted
* Where an airway has 2 types (AIRWAY and TMZ) it has been entered twice.
*

***********************************************************
* Part 2 ENR section 5.4                                  *
*   Air navigation obstacles                              *
***********************************************************
*
* This section of the AIP consists of a spreadsheet with over 4700 entries.
* By far the largest entry is for wind turbines, which account for 3904.
* Rather than try and determine what should or shouldn't be included, in this
* section of this file I've only copied the entries in PD's / RO's files and
* applied any location / height corrections.  These are primarily the Radio
* Transmitter Masts and Chimneys
*
* The spreadsheet was updated in 2016 - it now runs to over 6000 entries
